text:
WOW this was good. I followed posters suggestions and used 2C water and dissolved a boulion cube in it. I also added a little white wine, the garlic and a shallot to deglaze the pan b4 adding the water/spice mixture. Even then, I had to add about a cup more water while it was cooking. I also dredged the chik breasts in a lemon pepper seasoning in addition to the oregono. I omitted all the salt from the recipe too, since boulion is so salty. Made the leftover broth into gravy, cooked up the Uncle Bens Chicken rice, and dinner was AbFab!! I will def be making this again!

Easy and moist.  I did as others suggested and added more liquids: 1/2 c chicken broth, 1/3 lemon juice, and since I had it on hand, about 1/2 c white wine.  When ready to plate, I thickened sauce with cornstarch.  It was great over egg noodles! Took less than 3 hrs. in crockpot.

text:
This chicken is truly delicious.  I have made this recipe four or five times already, it's definitely a keeper.  It doesn't make much extra sauce so if you want some to scoop over potatoes or pasta you should double the sauce.  The only thing I do differently is I use boneless skinless chicken tenders instead of chicken breast halves.  The chicken pieces are smaller which allows them to soak up more of the juices and seasonings making them very flavorful and tender.  I have also added sliced mushrooms... yum.

text:
My first crock pot experience, and it turned out great! I took a lot of advice from the posts here: I covered the bottom of the pot with potatoes, onions, mushrooms, and lots of garlic (about 6 cloves). I used bone-in breasts (I did brown them first, using butter, salt and lemon-pepper mix, awesome), then deglazed the pan with 1 cup white wine. Added all that to the pot, along with 2 cans of chicken stock, 6 tablespoons lemon juice, and a little more salt. I cooked on high for 2 hours, then low for 1 hour - perfect! I think the bone-in chicken made a big difference, it was wonderful and falling apart. I would be careful with the lemon juice - I love strong flavors and was tempted to add more, but my 6 tablespoons was bordering on too bitter - excellent though! Also turned the extra juice into gravy for veggies and it was yummy, with side of chicken couscous!

text:
What a dish!  I doubled the spices except the garlic and used the juice of an entire lemon, and used chicken stock instead of water/boullion, using enough stock to almost cover chicken.  And 30 min. before cook time finished, I stirred in 2 T. cornstarch dissolved in 1/4 cup water.  Plenty of sauce for serving with chicken over pasta.  And here's a trick:  it was REALLY lemony and too sour, so I stirred in almost 2 T sugar.  Totally fixed that problem.  It was DIVINE!!!  Thanks for an awesome, interesting recipe.

text:
THis turned out surprisingly good!!! I used two boneless skinless breasts, (1lb) and I did everything by the recipe except used more garlic as we LOVE garlic...I used the already minced garlic...I also took everyone elses advice & used chicken broth instead of water...I made enough to cover chicken so it did not dry out...I also cooked this for about 4 1/2 hours on low.....I took juice out of crockpot, added cornstarch to thicken it up & made a yummy gravy! returned gravy & chicken to crockpot & left on warm..chicken fell apart & soaked in so much flavor it was unreal! I served w/Uncle Ben's whole grain brown rice w/garlic flavors & steamed broccoli & cauliflower & it was sensational! My fiance is NOT a big chicken eater & he ate every bite of his & complimented the flavor! Will definitely make again...I def. agree that making sure the breasts are covered in liquid is key..also, my chicken breast were kind of thick & so I think this helped it not to dry out! Sooo yummy!

text:
After reading a few reviews, this is what I did - 3 pounds of chicken (family packs on sale here!) seasoned with salt, pepper and oregano. Browned in butter. 1 14 oz can chicken broth, 4 tbsp lemon juice (from the bottle) and 3 cloves minced refrigerated garlic. 1 hour on high. 3 hours on low. 30 minutes before serving, mixed 2 tbsp cornstarch with 1/4 cup water and poured over the top. This was absolutely some of the best chicken I have ever tasted. My whole family loved it. And the sauce was so good I could've just eaten a bowl of it like soup! Seriously good stuff.

This came out excellent with modifications! The amount of seasonings in the recipe is not nearly enough. ( I DID LEAVE OUT THE SALT!) I sprinkled onion pwder on the chicken as well before browning. I added more oregano, garlic and pepper - didn't measure, just went by eye & to my liking. I added a 1/2 sweet onion, fresh basil, juiced one whole lemon, added one cup white wine & added about 3 tablespoons fresh parsley. I also used a cup of chicken broth AND a 1/2 teaspoon of chicken boullion for extra flavor. It came out PERFECT and was not salty AT ALL!! Great, GREAT flavor!! Served it over a brown rice mix. =) YUM!

This dish was very, very good. I omitted the water and bouillon and used 1/4 cup of chicken broth instead, and it worked wonderfully. The garlic and lemon truly infuse the chicken, which becomes incredibly tender in the slow cooker. My only caveat would be that the chicken was somewhat bland--it's not a very piquant dish. (I'm love strong flavors, but this isn't a characteristic slow cooking usually imparts.) Nonetheless, I'll definitely make this again.

text:
This was terrific! The chicken was so moist and just fell apart.  I cooked it on high for 3 hours. I did make 2 cups of chicken broth, the juice from one lemon, 4 cloves of garlic and some white wine. I forgot to boil that mixture before putting it in the crock pot, but I can't tell what I was missing. The key is browning the chicken before putting it into the pot. I would suggest using olive oil instead of butter and putting the garlic in for the last 2 minutes to get the full flavor. I also shred the chicken and let it soak up the juices for awhile before serving - yummy! We used the juice to pour over the chicken. This was a great meal to come home to with hardly any effort! It will be in my monthly dishes from now on.

text:
I put this recipe in my box 3 years ago...I finally cooked it over the weekend and it was phenomenal!  Like other reviewers, I doubled (should have tripled) the liquid ingredients.  My slow cooker is pretty strong, so I cooked mine on Low for 4 hours, rotating the chicken halfway through the cycle so that the chicken on top would get in the juices.  After 2 hours, the chicken was falling apart it was so tender!  I removed the chicken from the juices, added a couple of tablespoons of cornstarch and made a fabulous gravy.  Served it over egg noodles with steamed broccoli.  It was a crowd pleaser!  And the little leftovers there were, the chicken was still tender when re-heated!

We gave this five stars, although I took a lot of suggestions along the way!  First, didn't bother browning the chicken.  Second, omitted the salt and bouillon/water and used a can of chicken broth and a glug or two of white wine.  Third, used lemon pepper instead of regular and used a whole teaspoon.  Put it all into the crock pot and cooked two hours on high and two and a half on low.  It came out pretty well, although next time I might try putting in some of the lemon zest to give it a little bit more lemon flavor.  Thanks!

This is healthy, easy and fast, inexpensive and delicious... a 5 star rating for sure! I make this alot, the only change that I make is that I just throw everything in the crock pot without browning or boiling and let the crock pot do it's work. I usually shred it a bit and serve over whole-grain thin pasta noodles or egg noodles and it's fantastic! This is comfort food, not spicy or over the top...so if you are looking for a "wow" your guests recipe, this is not the one. It's just great family food. Perfect for a cold day like today!

I know that a lot of people don't really like it when people change a bunch of stuff in the recipe then review it. Well, sorry, cause that's exactly what I did and it was really good. I basically took the advice of others by adding wine (1/2 cup), doubling the sauce (used 1 can chik broth), etc. I always have a batch of my homemade seasoned flour on hand, so I used that and added extra Oregano. I added some sauteed onions and extra garlic in with the chicken. the last 30 minutes I added a can of Artichoke hearts ( the kind in water, but drained) and some Capers. I adjusted the salt in the recipe accordingly, by the way. I thickened the sauce a bit with some cornstarch and I swirled in about a tbsp of butter right before serving. I served it over Linguine and a bed of fresh spinach. The sauce and chicken wilted the spinach a bit, but it was still a bit crunchy. We sprinkled Feta and Parm chz on top. Everyone liked this, even picky kids. Going into the rotaion for sure!  Oh -it was done on high in about 2 hours, 45 minutes. turned it on warm till we were ready- The chicken was done prefectly!

text:
Made this for dinner last night, and it was really VERY good. I omitted the oregano (we hate oregano), reamed a large lemon for 4 tbs of juice and pulp instead of juice only, used Better Than Bullion bullion paste, added 3 oz of chopped shallots and an extra clove of garlic when deglazing the pan, and used Smart Balance instead of butter to help cut down on the fat. I also added 1/2 c water to the slow cooker and let it cook on high for about 5 hours. My house smelled amazing all day, and dinner did not disappoint! I served it with steamed broccoli and lemon butter rice, which was especially good with the sauce from the chicken. We wished there was more. I think I will follow others' suggestion of white wine when deglazing to help bolster the amount. The chicken was slightly dry, so next time I will cut the cook time down to four hours. And there *will* be a next time. I've already been asked by my husband to add it to the dinner rotation! Thanks to Carla Joe for sharing this recipe and to all the reviewers who shared their suggestions. Great communal effort with a wonderful outcome. :-)

text:
I found this recipe and it seemed simple enough. Many (MANY )of the readers recommended I tweak the recipe, which I did. I added a 2 tsp of olive oil to the butter, bc as one reader said it wouldn't have been enough to brown. I also used a lemon pepper seasoned salt from Goya instead to season the chicken before I browned it. I also let the pan get a little brown(yummy brown, not eww, its burned brown) on the bottom and deglazed it with chicken broth and added it to the crock pot. (I find that gives it the best flavor!) I don't like using bouillon cubes, so I added 2 cups of chicken broth, like many of the readers recommended. I added Italian seasonings (rosemary, thyme, oregano, parsley flakes) on top of the chicken. I love garlic and onions, so I used half a small onion (chopped) and used 6 garlic cloves (minced). Then I squeezed a whole lemon into the crock pot and added the squeezed lemon pieces in. I like doing this because it gives in a real lemon-y flavor. I also added 1/4 cup of balsamic vinegar which a few readers recommended as well. It took about 30 mins prep time. I am cooking the chicken on high for 6 hours. I love things fully cooked, so I would rather have it fall apart than be underdone. I will probably add some potatoes and serve over rice. :)

text:
Awesome, easy and DELICIOUS! A definite "keeper." My only suggestion is for people who have a large slow cooker (mine is a 6-qt.) you may want to make 2-3 times as much of the lemon juice mixture as the amount suggested in the recipe, as that much barely even wet the bottom of my cooker. As a result the chicken was a little drier than I expected. But the flavor was still wonderful! Went great over rice with brocolli on the side. BTW for those of you watching your fat intake, you can add the lemon juice mixture directly to the slow cooker, without mixing in the pan drippings, and it tastes exactly the same. (Discovered this by accident when I forgot that step!)

country:
None
text:
Tried this great recipe yesterday and it was great. I made a few changes to the original recipe after reading most of the reviews. 
1. I used adobo seasoning (Goya, garlic powder, oregano along with some freshly squezzed orange juice and let it sit in the fridge for 2+ hours before cooking. No need to brown the chicken prior to cooking.
2. I used homemade broth from a previous recipe that I saved to use it later ( definetly a time saver, and taste saver too!)
3. After cooking the garlic, lemon juice and the broth I strained the garlic from the skillet. That way the liquid had only the flavor of the garlic instead of overpowdering it. 
4. Once in the slow cooker, I added baby carrots and peas. they were cooked in the amazing broth and came in super tender, also the chicken was in the broth and came out with amazing flavor, juicy and very very tender. 

My family loved this recipe with the modifications I did. Hope this helps others and like I always say do not be afraid to modify a recipe, most times it is just a guide. Enjoy!!

Yum!  Lots of flavor in this dish.  The only changes I made were 1) I used the juice of two lemons (a little more than 3 T.)  After browning the chicken (I used 5 fat breasts cut in half), I deglazed the skillet with bouillion dissolved in about a cup of hot water, about a half cup of chicken broth, lemon juice, garlic and I also added about a cup of white wine.  These ingredients were boiled together and poured over the chicken in the crock pot.  I cooked the chicken in the crock pot for about 7 hours on low.  I served this with penne pasta sprinkled with parmeson and green beans.  My family loved it.

text:
I have been searching for slow cooker chicken recipes that don't require cream soups or other processed foods, and this one seemed to fit the bill.  It was decent, but nothing spectacular.  I made a few changes which I think made it much better.  I used olive oil instead of butter.  I deglazed the pan with 1/2 cup white wine (pinot grigio) then added 1 cup chicken broth.  Since I cooked only 4 chicken breasts (about 1 lb.) this was enough liquid to cover them in the slow cooker.  I kept the other ingredient amounts the same.  I cooked it on high for 3 hours, removed the chicken and added a corn starch slurry (2 Tbsp. corn starch in 2 Tbsp. water) to thicken up the sauce and served it all over angel hair pasta.  It came out a little bland and dry.  I think I will make this again, but maybe season the chicken with "Chicken Seasoning Blend" from this site to perk it up.

text:
This was a very easy and tasty slow cooker chicken recipe, just what I have been looking for.  I used a whole cut-up chicken, with the skin removed, and the meat just fell off the bone.  I love garlic, so I added 2 teaspoons of minced, and I used fresh lemon juice, but other than that, I didn't change a thing.  I did find that after browning the meat, it didn't take 6 hours to cook on low, it was more like 4 1/2, but with all the liquid, the meat didn't dry out.  I also used my fat skimming measuring cup to get rid of the small amount of chicken fat, and then used cornstarch to thicken the gravy, making it a relatively low fat dish.  Would be very good over egg noodles.  Thanks for the recipe!

This was very, very good. A nice change from the creamy chicken recipes. A few tips for first timers like me:
-Don't use too much rub on the chicken. I figured most of it would come off while cooking, so I used a lot, but it all stayed on!
-Like a lot of the comments on here, I added another 1/2 cup water and 1/2 tsp chicken granules and 2 tblsps lemon juice to make more juice.
-Next time, I will cut down on the garlic just a little.
I forgot to do the parsley and after all of these changes, it was a great meal with white rice--just perfect!

text:
I had a dish at a diner called Chicken Diane & it was so amazing... I've never been able to find it again OR find a recipe - and this recipe is spot on with a few additions per the suggestions of the other chef n' raters:

1st step: used garlic pepper and kosher salt instead of just salt and pepper. Oregano as indicated.

2nd step: I used 2 cups of chicken broth and 1/2 cup of white wine, 4 tsps of jarred garlic, juice from one whole large lemon. Follow rest per recipe.

3rd step: take a strained 4 oz jar of Goya artichoke hearts and 6 oz of fresh mushrooms with chicken breasts in cooker on low for 1 hour and high for 1 hour. There will be a lot of sauce so after its cooked take the meat and vegs out of liquid and on stove with 3 tbsp of corn starch to thicken then back into crock pot for 30 minutes.I took 1 whole cup of the sauce in this liquid and added it to the rice. AMAZING AND LEMONY. Tasted just like the diner I ate at. Nailed it.

text:
The only modifications I made was that I added capers and scallions, used an Italian herb blend as opposed to just oregano and I cooked it with the lemon. As others suggested I increased the liquid by deglazing the pan with 1/2 cup white cooking wine and 1 cup water. Although the chicken was very tender, it did have a bit of a bitter after-taste and the liquid was so bitter I didn't bother trying to thicken it in a gravy. Maybe it was because I threw the lemon in the crock pot-- but it just had a bad bitter taste. Be careful about how much lemon you use. I wish I would have heeded the warnings of others about this. Not sure if I'll try it again.

text:
I have made this recipe twice.  The first time, I made it as directed, except, I used canned chicken stock and juice of 1& 1/2 lemons (didn't measure the amount of juice).  I added everything to the slow cooker- and I thought the chicken was a bit dried out- but with good flavor.  The sauce did NOT cover all the chicken- that's why I think it dried out.
Then last night I made the recipe again...but rather than putting it all into the slow cooker, I removed the browned chicken from the fry pan, then  added the liquid ingredients to the fry pan to deglaze, and then returned the chicken to the original fry pan, covered it, reduced the heat, and let it all simmer until the chicken was cooked through.  Once the chicken was cooked all through (about 20 minutes), I again removed the chicken to a serving dish,and then added a bit of corn starch to thicken the sauce.  I tasted it- it was a bit strong- so I added a bit of water to dilute.  I poured the sauce over the chicken and served with broccoli and rice.  Totally gone!  Now, not THE VERY BEST- but very quick, easy, and the gang ate it up!  I will definately make again...just without the slow cooker!

This smelled fantastic while it was cooking, and was fall-apart tender when served.  Contrary to what other reviewers have said, it is very important to brown the chicken before putting it in the crock pot - this seals in the juices so the meat stays moist and tender.  I do have to say, though, that flavor-wise it seemed like something was missing, although I can't really put my finger on it.  Maybe some onion (or a tsp or two of onion soup mix)?  I served it with rice and steamed veggies.  It really was good, but just seemed to need a little something to complete the flavor.  I will definitely make it again, but play around with the recipe to see if I can figure out what's missing.

text:
Pretty good.  You can hardly go wrong with a crock pot recipe!  Due to some of the reviews, I doubled the sauce and threw the ingredients in a pan and boiled for a bit, added a can of chicken broth, and then poured it on top of my salted and peppered chicken breasts (I did not want to precook the chicken.)  It cooked up nicely in the crock pot (mine was not dry at all as I had enough liquid to completely cover the chicken and I cooked it 8 hours on low,) but I found it to be too lemony so I added just a bit of sugar, maybe one tsp, and a nice couple of shakes of garlic powder as you could not taste the garlic at all.  After it was done, I poured the juices from the chicken back into a pan to come to a quick boil and thickened it with corn starch.  It was still pretty lemony but it went well served over egg noodles.  It was a nice lite tasting summer dish which all enjoyed.  Thank you!

text:
I have the tendency to not follow the AMOUNT of the given ingredients and this recipe was no exception, but it turned out GREAT! With the dry ingredients, I kind of just dumped, tapped or sprinkled depending what I felt it needed. I also used 5 chicken breasts because of my family size, which is more than 2 pounds, so obviously I had to adjust the ingredients. For the one person that I saw that complained of it being dry, it's because they DIDN'T brown it first because apparently the don't know how to add extra butter. The browning it gives it a solid outside and seals in the moisture. I used EXTRA butter and it sealed in the moisture GREAT. This was moist, juicy and tasted FANTASTIC! This has been added to our favorite meals! I also used jarred garlic instead of cloves. Don't know if that made a difference but once again, it tasted FANTASTIC!

text:
Quite unlike the moist chicken promised by the recipe, my chicken was so dry it was difficult to eat. Instead of serving the breasts as the center of the meal, I improvised and heated the cooking liquid on the stove, turning it into a soup broth. I added chicken stock, some honey, and thickened the mixture with two egg yolks. I poured the broth over the shredded chicken, steamed carrots, and brown rice. In the end, it was good, but quite different from the original recipe. I recommend dramatically reducing the cook time for tender chicken--no more than 4 hrs on low heat.

Yum! Yum! Yum!  We did make the following alterations: used garlic salt instead of salt, doubled the lemon juice, put in 2 cups of water and 2 chicken bouillon cubes, and used a pinch of dried parsley instead of the fresh. text:
This was pretty good, the meat fell off the bone (I used bone-in breasts) and there was plenty of flavor, but I agree that the liquid amounts need to be adjusted so that the meat is covered in the pot. I threw some sliced onion and baby carrots in the bottom and cooked on low for 6 hours; I think 5 would have been a little better. It tasted just like mom's homemade chicken soup - nothing wrong with that! - but if you're looking for something fancier, you might be a little let down by this one. Adding white wine really gives it a nice touch. I'll be making it again soon, thanks for the recipe!

I was looking for a chicken crock pot recipe that didn't have the cream soup as most do and I think this is a very tasty one. As others suggested, I used a half cup of chicken broth instead of the water and buillon. I also increased the lemon juice to 4 tbsp. I used italian seasoning instead of the oregano which I liked very much. I cooked it on low and checked it after it cooked for a little over 4 hours and found that it was already done (actually maybe just a little overcooked as it was starting to dry out). Although I was only cooking 2 chicken breasts. But other than being a little dry, it tasted great. I served it with white rice and asparagus and it made a woderful meal.

I made this tonight, and everybody loved how it turned out.  Tender chicken, great flavor!  I served it over angel hair pasta and sprinkled a little Locatelli cheese on top...Yum! I am definitely adding this to my list of go-to dinners. :)

text:
We really didn't like this. It had no flavor and was dry. I followed the recipe exactly, except I used chicken tenderloins, instead of breast halves, because they were cheaper, and I forgot to add the parsley at the end. Served it with angel hair pasta with parmesan cheese, and steamed broccoli. I was going to thicken the sauce this makes to go over the noodles, but hated the flavor of it, so I cracked open a bottle of alfredo sauce. The only way we could eat this was to mix it in with the pasta. That said, I do think it has potential to be good.  Next time I make this, I will do the following: marinade the chicken for at least an hour in the juice of one lemon, olive oil, two cloves of garlic, garlic salt, lemon pepper, and oregano.  Then, I will either do the entire thing in the slow cooker, without browning the chicken first, or I will do the entire thing on the stove top. If I go with the slow cooker method, I will cook on low for no more than 4 hours. I will also use chicken broth, instead of water and bouillon, use lemon pepper instead of black pepper, and garlic salt instead of regular salt. I do think this particular recipe would be better done on the stove top because being able to scrape the brown bits into the sauce will help boost flavor, but both methods are unnecessary and results in dry chicken. Also, 6 hours for chicken is way, way too long. I never go more than 4. But I always follow the recipe the first time.

text:
I doubled the seasonings adding 1 tsp. lemon peel or zest of one lemon and only 1/2 tsp. salt to the mixture  to coat the chicken, then browned.   I used 1 cup chicken broth instead of boullion and 1/4 cup lemon wine instead of water (deglazed the pan with the wine).  I also used a whole lemon. Juiced it then layered the chicken in the crockpot with onion, garlic, additional fresh oregano sprigs and the lemon remains cut in wedges making sure chicken is covered with broth.  Used chicken thighs and after 3 hours on low the chicken fell apart.  Thickened the gravy/sauce with cornstarch aND lemon juice.  Served it over mashed potatoes made with butter and sour cream.  Very tender, moist and deliciously lemony.  Husband says it would also be excellent served over egg noodles, rigatoni, any pasta or rice.  Plan to  to try with potatoes, onion, carrots, and a little fennel.

text:
Basically same recipe, but modified to make it easier, removed salt.
Filet 2-3 Chicken Breasts into 2 pieces each.
Sprinkle to coat both sides with equal portions Lemon Pepper and Oregano.  Brown only lightly in butter.
In slow cooker MIX 1-2 cups low sodium chicken broth, 2 cloves chopped Garlic , 1 tsp Parsley, 3 TBsp lemon juice.  Arrange chicken in slow cooker so they are all submerged; add more broth if necessary.  Cook low 6-8 hrs, server over egg noodles or rice.  Broth can be thickened after for a more gravy like result.  YUMMM.

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I didn't  have fresh lemons in the house so I used lemon juice. Additionally, I used minced garlic from a jar because my garlic press recently broke. I can imagine this dish would be even more heavenly with the fresh ingredients. Here's what I did: once the chicken has been cooking in the crockpot for 45 minutes, I melted 4 tablespoons of butter in a saucepan over medium heat, not allowing it to brown. Then add 2 1/2 cups of water, 3 more tablespoons of lemon juice, 1 1/2 tsp of chicken bouillon and 2 tsp minced garlic and allow it to come to a boil. Remove from heat immediately and pour over the chicken in the crockpot. Be sure to make sure the chicken isn't sticking to the bottom and stir the liquid, being sure to scrape the bottom to incorporate the browning chicken. Twenty minutes before it was done cooking, I added the fresh parsley as directed. Before serving, I pulled the chicken apart a little bit, then served the chicken and its broth over my favorite Basmati Rice. Hope this helps.

text:
Followed suggestions of doubling liquid. Great idea as this sauce is wow! Also cooked on low, this helps keep the chicken moist. Another tip for slow cooking is not to open the cover too much during cooking as the steam, moisture inside will come out. This is what cooks and keeps meats moist in a slow cooker. This is not a dish that adapts well to all-day cooking but I think it is a great last minute idea (3-4 hours on LOW is perfect). Thanks!

I have to give this a 5 star, the chicken was so tender and worth the wait. I cooked it on low for about 4 hours and it was done. I also added chicken broth to the slow cooker and made sure that all the chicken was covered. A few people were saying that it was dry because not enough juice. I have to say, you must add chicken broth. I also doubled up the rub and I served it with mashed potatoes and put the extra juice over the potatoes. This is a excellent chicken dish. Quick to assemble, easy, but the wait. Well that is what a slow cooker is for. :)

text:
This was the second time I've tried this recipe, both times it has come out FANTASTIC. 

The first time was in the crockpot....took a bit longer to cook than the recipe said, maybe an extra hour or so, and I didn't think there was enough liquid (although what there was, was delicious, just not enough for the rice I served with it!)

This time I only doubled the water and chicken boullion (1/2 cup water & 2 tsp boullion) and one extra tbsp of lemon juice (all I had left).  I started it too late in the day for the slowcooker, so I did everything the same, except after browning the chicken and adding the liquid, I then placed it all in a baking pan, covered it tightly in foil, then baked it for an hour at 350.  It came out wonderfully moist and very tasty.

This is a permanent 'regular' for our family...my husband and all the kids (4 of them ranging from 2 to 12) ALL cleaned their plates!

text:
I took the advice from the accompanying video and increased the spices on the chicken.  Didn't really make a lot of difference after the chicken had been in the sauce for all that time.  The chicken was pretty tasteless.  I removed the mushrooms and the chicken from the slow cooker, transferred the liquid to a saute pan and reduced by 1/3.  I adjusted for salt and added garlic salt as well.  Originally, it was t was very lemony, but the garlic was virtually non-existent.  The garlic salt in the end made all the difference, as well as the corn starch to thicken the sauce to a more gravy-like consistency.  I wish I had made mashed-potatoes.  The gravy, in the end, was AMAZING.  I encourage everyone to shred the chicken, in order to take as much gravy as possible per bite.  YUMMY!!!

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
Tweaks:
*Add 1/4 t. Lemon Pepper to rub mixture
*Use 1/4 c. White Wine to deglaze pan
*Substitute 2c. Chicken Stock for water/bouillon
*Add 1 chopped Shallot to stock mixture
*Adjust salt of stock sauce, to taste
*Before serving, remove chicken from sauce and thicken sauce with mixture of 1/4 c. Water w/ 2T. Corn Starch. Low boil until thickened, then return chicken to pot and top w/ parsley.
*Serve over Easy Brown Rice
*Recipe also works on stovetop in heavy dutch  oven lidded pot

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
We loved this recipe at our house and will definitely make it again.  I followed many of the other reviewers and used:  3 cloves minced garlic, 1 small shallot minced, 1 cup chicken stock, 1/2 - 3/4 tbsp Better Than Bouillon Chicken Base instead of the crystals (seems to have less sodium), 3 tbsp fresh lemon juice, 1/4 c white wine- and used this mixture to deglaze the pan after browning the chicken.  I used chicken tenders instead of breasts which definitely allowed more of the seasoning to seep into the meat during the slow cooking process.  In addition to the above  ingredients, I also used approximately 1/2 - 3/4 tsp white pepper to add a little kick.  Cooked on high for the first hour, and then 3 hours on low.  When I had 30 minutes left, I added 2 tbsp of cornstarch and thickened the liquid.  I did add some extra chicken stock to make sure the meat was fully submersed in the liquid during cooking.  Served with mashed potatoes and spinach- delightful!

text:
Awesome recipe. However, as usual I put my spin on it with limited resources & counter space. If you like, you can prepare the chicken breasts (also works with pork chops) remove some of the fat & you can thin the breasts (optional) for faster cooking. Put some Olive oil in pan with minced garlic & sliced onion until garlic starts to brown. Season chicken with seasoned salt & lemon pepper & place in pan add lemon juice and about 1/4 cup of beer & cook over medium heat until chicken is done. The fluids will be absorbed & evaporate allowing a sear if desired. Keep a close eye on chicken breasts, they have a tendency to be a little dry if over cooked. Note: You can use the lemon juice, garlic, seasoned salt, lemon pepper, onion & beer as a marinade which will leave you with the option to cook inside or BBQ. Hope this works for you.

text:
This came out so much better than anticipated! I followed a previous poster and deglazed the pan with white onion (what I had at home already), fresh minced garlic, and sherry (I was out of vermouth which is my go-to). I slowly added the lemon juice from there and pre dissolved the bouillon in warm water then added it to the onion mixture in pan to boil. I added basil and fill to the chicken rub which added a nice burst of flavor on top of the juice. Definitely make extra juice, I served this with a Greek style potato salad and the juice was an amazing addition to that. I doubled the garlic all around since we're garlic lovers. I thought I cooked the chicken too much and thought it would be dry since it was completely done (1.5lbs chicken) in the crock in about two hours and left to sit another 4 before dinner. I was wrong! Super moist, tender, and fell apart when stabbed with a fork! Packed with flavor, definitely making this again and possibly adding capers over pasta. Yum!

Really good tasting recipe, but there are a few adjustments that need to be made.  I cooked on low for 5 1/2 hours and probably that was 30 minutes too long.  The 1/4 cup water called for was not nearly enough.  I used 1/2 cup and will add an additional 1/4 cup if I make this again. I made this for my husband the other night, and he really enjoyed it. I used Mrs. Dash Original for the spices since husband is watching sodium intake. I also followed others' advice and added more liquid in the form of white wine and salt-free chicken bullion dissolved in water, 1 cup each. text:
First time making lemon chicken -- or even eating it for that matter --and the family really liked it. Tried to followed the recipe with the following exceptions (mostly because a lot of reviewers said it was bland):

- Pounded chicken breasts thin to help cook more evenly/faster
-  added basil to the spices
- used fresh juice from 3 lemons
- used 2 15 oz cans chicken broth (instead of water & bullion), we like extra sauce
- thickened sauce with corn starch
- baked in oven at 350 for 30 minutes (didn't have time for crockpot but will try it that way eventually)

Served with plain spaghetti noodles, steamed broccoli and garlic bread...oh and fresh Parmesan sprinkled on top.

Thanks for another meal in the rotation.

text:
Great recipe with a couple of tweaks. I used lemon & pepper seasoning instead of the salt, pepper and oregano since we are not fans of oregano, doubled the sauce using all chicken broth instead of water, a lot more garlic and lemon, and I also cut the very thick chicken breasts into 3" pieces before sauting. I browned all sides to lock in the juices and then cooked for 6 hours on low. Just before serving I added cornstarch to thicken the sauce and I served with steamed rice and steamed broccoli w/lemon that I mixed together and my family wants it again tonight!  What a cost effective, hearty and delicious meal!

This dish satisfied all the family members. My husband and daughter are more "plain" eaters and do not like gravies or sauces. I, however am in the category of more sauce the better. I made this dish according to others suggestions and added white wine along with more liquids. At the end of the cooking time I took the breasts out to keep warm and made of slurry of milk and corn starch to add to the liquid in the crockpot and turned it to high to thicken. It was a delicious chicken herb gravy.  I got my sauce and the rest of the family loved the chicken. Served with mashed potatoes and green beans it was an easy and tasty Sunday supper.

It was great! After reading reviews I used 1/2c water, 1/2c white wine, 2 packets of bouillon, 3 cloves of garlic and thin cut chicken cutlets. I did not brown the chicken before but I heated the liquids and garlic then just poured over the chicken. Cooked on high for 2.5 hours and it came out perfectly. I also added cornstarch in the last 30 mins. to thicken the sauce. It was excellent but I wish there was more sauce! I will definitely add more liquid next time. I also would have liked more of a lemon taste so I will add more of that next time as well. Served over angel hair pasta. Highly recommend; very flavorful.

text:
I've made this twice so far, once per the recipe. Second time I cooked the chicken for 15min on a stovetop pressure cooker, and it came out the same (easy to fork-shred, infused with flavor). To facilitate this I used 1cup water, 3T lemon, and still just 1 chicken pellet. Quick-release the steam, then return to a near boil uncovered for a few minutes, mixing in the parsley and optional cornstarch.  The extra sauce was great over mashed potatoes. Sauted shrooms were also a good addition. 

Great for leftovers - stuff into a pita with hummus, olives, and rice, or shred the chicken and make a panini.

I added more liquid as suggested by other reviewers, so that I could turn it into some sauce for pasta.  I used one cup of water with a teaspoon of chicken bouillon granules.  I cooked it on high for 3 hours, then low for one hour.  The chicken was nice and tender, not too overcooked.  I felt it was very salty, so I added half a cup of water, then used half a cup of water with cornstarch to thicken it up for sauce.  This evened out the salt.  My husband loved it, but I thought it was just ok.  If I make it again, I will leave out the oregano, as I felt that was an overpowering flavor for this.

text:
This was SO good and SO easy!  I did make a couple changes, probably doesn't need them, but I always tweak recipes a bit.   I used a mix of butter and olive oil to brown chicken.  After browned I sauteed some onion and I used TONS of garlic, my family thinks the more the better!   I also zested a lemon, along with the lemon juice and used homemade chicken broth (2 cups instead of 1) instead of water and bouillon.  And I added a couple tablespoons of capers and poured a bit of caper juice in.  I let all this simmer for a few minutes and then poured it over chicken in slow cooker.   When it was ready, I made some plain arborio rice according to directions.  I served by shredding the chicken, mixing that with all the broth/cooking juice and the rice.  I get RAVE reviews for all who try it...it is even better second (third day)!

I made this twice now and it just gets better with practice. I changed it up as others had. 1/2 cup of riesling wine, 2 cups of water, 4 teaspoons of minced garlic from a jar, 1/4 cup of lemon juice from a bottle, 3 teaspoons of bouillon, and one package of McCormick's chicken gravy.

My Modifications:
Zest of 1 lemon.

After seeing that the juice mixture does not cover the chicken:
Melt 2 TBSP of butter,
Mix in 2 TBSP of flour,
Add 1 can chicken broth,
Add seasoning (Oregano, Salt, Pepper, Garlic Powder, etc),
Bring to boil while mixing,

Add to Chicken.

text:
I tried this chicken tonight and it turned out really good. I used 5 frozen chicken breasts and thawed them out just enough for the oregano and garlic to stick. I didn't really measure any of the ingredients. I used about a tbsp. of oregano, 2 cloves of garlic and the juice from two lemons. I was worried the garlic would be too much, but it had a nice flavor. I used 2 tsp of concentrated bouillon liquid and 1 cup of water. I also sprinkled some lemon pepper seasoning on it before adding the liquid in the slow cooker. I cooked it on low for about 4 hrs and the chicken was still partially frozen when I started. My picky ten year old recommends that I make it again, so I say that's a win

text:
I made quite a few changes. No bouillon which eliminated the high sodium (yay!). Sprayed bottom of crock pot w/ olive oil Pam. Placed a layer of onion (1 whole good size onion total in recipe) & chopped garlic (2 bunches of cloves total in recipe); laid the chicken breast on top of those; placed more onion & garlic on top of chicken; added 4 mushrooms, thickly sliced, sprinkled basil, rosemary, & oregano then squeezed a whole lemon and dropped the rinds on top. Poured a 1/2 cup white wine & 1 cup low sodium chicken stock over everything. Cooked on Low for 7 hours. 
Super juicy and full of rich flavors

text:
It came out a bit like a soup, but I did 2.5x the recipe, so that might be why. 
I used ~4c water and 1c white wine and 2 bullion cubes. 
It wasn't too salty, but it probably would have been fine without the salt anyway. 
I also added 2 tbsp almond flour at the end to give some substance to the broth.
The chicken was super tender.
I'd be curious to follow the recipe more strictly, but I was just worried that with some of the chicken in the broth and some of it out (within the crockpot), it wouldn't all get cooked/tender to the same degree.

Really enjoyed this recipe :). I too upped the liquid levels; with which I later added 1 1/2 tbsp xanthan gum to in order to thicken it up into a gravy-like mix. I added small whole potatoes, sliced carrots, & diced celery to the slowcooker pot as well. 2 1/2 hrs on high, and another hour on low = nicely cooked chicken that fell apart on my fork hehe. I wanna try this again with bone-in breasts & legs some time; or just a whole chicken. I added a photo compilation as well ;)

*Tip: be mindful of the spices. I added a bit too much pepper since I thought it seemed 'light', WHOOO it left a 'hot' sensation on my tongue after eating haha. Not a big deal to be honest, just thought I'd mention to not over-add more spices/seasonings unless you want a stronger flavor from em.

All in all, this is a keeper recipe for me.

text:
This was excellent!  I usually don't do chicken breasts in the crock pot because they get too dry, but these stayed nice and moist and the flavor was delicious.  As per some of the other reviews, I used a can of chicken broth in place of the water and granules.  I also doubled the oregano, salt, and pepper rub, but I don't think I will do that again because I think it made the chicken a bit too "spicy" for my kids and they wouldn't eat it.  However, I will be making this again.  
definitely make this again.

text:
Very well recieved by my family. I had to double the herb mixture and I added a can of chicken broth as well as the chicken granules.  I thought it was a little salty, so I'll omit the salt next time.  I'll also add 2 cans of chicken broth, as it didn't have enough sauce. Served it with buttered rice and made a tossed green salad and broccoli for side dishes. My husband gave it a 10. This is a keeper and especially for the ease of this dish.  Thanks for sharing it. :-)
